             </span>
            </span>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=NASA+%E2%80%93+Phobos&amp;rft.pub=Solarsystem.nasa.gov&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsolarsystem.nasa.gov%2Fplanets%2Fprofile.cfm%3FObject%3DMar_Phobos&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APhobos+%28moon%29">
            <span style="display:none;">

           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/science/space/solarsystem/mars/phobos.shtml" rel="nofollow">
             "Phobos"
            </a>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Phobos&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fscience%2Fspace%2Fsolarsystem%2Fmars%2Fphobos.shtml&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APhobos+%28moon%29">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>

         <li id="cite_note-23">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-23">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.solarviews.com/cap/mars/phobos2.htm" rel="nofollow">
             "Stickney Crater-Phobos"
            </a>
            .
            <q>
             One of the most striking features of Phobos, aside from its irregular shape, is its giant crater Stickney. Because Phobos is only 28 by 20 kilometers (17 by 12 mi), it must have been nearly shattered from the force of the impact that caused the giant crater. Grooves that extend across the surface from Stickney appear to be surface fractures caused by the impact.
            </q>
           </cite>

         <li id="cite_note-27">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

             ^

           <cite class="citation journal">
            Ivanov, Andrei V. (March 2004). "Is the Kaidun Meteorite a Sample from Phobos?".
            <i>
             Solar System Research
            </i>
            .
            <b>
             38
            </b>
            (2): 97–107.
            <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">
             Bibcode
            </a>
            :
            <a class="external text" href="http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004SoSyR..38...97I" rel="nofollow">
             2004SoSyR..38...97I

            .
            <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
             doi
            </a>
            :
            <a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1023%2FB%3ASOLS.0000022821.22821.84" rel="nofollow">
             10.1023/B:SOLS.0000022821.22821.84
            </a>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Solar+System+Research&amp;rft.atitle=Is+the+Kaidun+Meteorite+a+Sample+from+Phobos%3F&amp;rft.volume=38&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=97-107&amp;rft.date=2004-03&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1023%2FB%3ASOLS.0000022821.22821.84&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2004SoSyR..38...97I&amp;rft.aulast=Ivanov&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrei+V.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APhobos+%28moon%29">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-28">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-28">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation journal">
            Ivanov, Andrei; Michael Zolensky (2003).
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.lpi.usra.edu/meetings/lpsc2003/pdf/1236.pdf" rel="nofollow">
             "The Kaidun Meteorite: Where Did It Come From?"
            </a>
            <span style="font-size:85%;">
             (PDF)
            </span>
            .
            <i>
             Lunar and Planetary Science
            </i>
            .
            <b>
             34
            </b>
            .
            <q>
             The currently available data on the lithologic composition of the Kaidun meteorite– primarily the composition of the main portion of the meteorite, corresponding to CR2 carbonaceous chondrites and the presence of clasts of deeply differentiated rock – provide weighty support for considering the meteorite’s parent body to be a carbonaceous chondrite satellite of a large differentiated planet. The only possible candidates in the modern Solar System are Phobos and Deimos, the moons of Mars.
            </q>
           </cite>
